      </div>

      <p><b>Kosovo</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>-/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Kosova</i> or <i lang="sq" title="Albanian-language text">Kosovë</i>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[kɔˈsɔva]</a></span> <span style="font-size:85%;">or</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[kɔˈsɔvə]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sr-Cyrl">Косово</span>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">[kôsoʋo]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Kosovo</b> (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Republika e Kosovës</i>; <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr"><span lang="sr-Cyrl" title="Serbian-language text">Република Косово</span> / <i lang="sr-Latn" title="Serbian-language text">Republika Kosovo</i></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">partially-recognised</a> <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disputed_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="Disputed territory">disputed territory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> On 17 February 2008, Kosovo unilaterally <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">declared its independence</a> from Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> It has since gained diplomatic recognition as a sovereign state by <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">98 UN member states</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Kosovo" title="Geography of Kosovo">Geographically</a> defined in an area of 10,887&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (4,203&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Kosovo is <a href="/wiki/Landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and bordered by the uncontested territory of Serbia to the north and east, <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> to the southwest and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> to the west. It possesses remarkable varied and diverse landscapes for its size by <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Kosovo" title="Climate of Kosovo">climate</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydrology" title="Hydrology">hydrology</a>. Most of central Kosovo is dominated by the vast plains and fields of <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_field_(Kosovo)" title="Kosovo field (Kosovo)">Kosovo</a>. The rugged <a href="/wiki/Prokletije" title="Prokletije">Prokletije</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar Mountains</a> rise in the southwest and southeast, respectively. </p>
      <p>Archaeological research has shown that the earliest known settlements in the territory of present-day Kosovo were linked to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Europe" title="Neolithic Europe">Neolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Star%C4%8Devo_culture" title="Starčevo culture">Starčevo culture</a> and the material culture groupins which succeeded it. The Bronze Age was marked by the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Balkan_languages" title="Paleo-Balkan languages">Indo-European tribes</a> and the appearance of <a href="/wiki/Tumuli" class="mw-redirect" title="Tumuli">tumuli</a>, a typical feature of Indo-European material culture, in existing and new sites. In classical antiquity, the central tribe which emerged in the territory of Kosovo was that of the <a href="/wiki/Dardani" title="Dardani">Dardani</a> who formed an independent polity known as the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dardania" title="Kingdom of Dardania">Kingdom of Dardania</a> in the 4th century BCE. Dardania was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> by the 1st century BCE and was later part of the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Praevalitana" title="Praevalitana">Praevalitana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Dardania</a>. Kosovo remained part of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">eastern Roman Empire</a> for over a thousand years. Byzantine administration was eroded by Slavic invasions beginning in the 6th-7th century AD. In the centuries thereafter control of the area alternated between the Byzantines and the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a>. By the 13th century, Kosovo became part of <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval Serbia">medieval Serbia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo</a> of 1389 is considered to be one of the defining moments in Serbian medieval history. The region was the core of the Serbian medieval state, which has also been the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a> from the 14th century, when its status was upgraded to a <a href="/wiki/Patriarchate" title="Patriarchate">patriarchate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Serbian_Empire" title="Fall of the Serbian Empire">fall of the Serbian Empire</a> in the late 14th century saw a quick succession of regional rulers until the 15th century when it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> until the early 20th century. </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo</a> 1389, the Serb medieval state survived for another 60 years, the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Despotate" title="Serbian Despotate">Serbian Despotate</a> became its successor. As a result, and leading up to the second <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo_(1448)" title="Battle of Kosovo (1448)">Battle of Kosovo (1448)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Despotate" title="Serbian Despotate">Serbian Despotate</a> deserted the anti-<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> cause and became an <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> vassal.<sup id="cite_ref-Malcolm_2002_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malcolm_2002-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some historians have argued the 1448 Battle of Kosovo, led by <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarian</a> leader <a href="/wiki/John_Hunyadi" title="John Hunyadi">John Hunyadi</a>, was the most important battle and defining moment in the region before final Ottoman occupation since it saw the last chance to expel the Ottomans.<sup id="cite_ref-Malcolm_2002_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malcolm_2002-15">[15]</a></sup> Anti-Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanian</a> forces led by <a href="/wiki/Skanderbeg" title="Skanderbeg">Skanderbeg</a> had planned to meet up with Hunyadi's forces in the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo field">Kosovo field</a> but were delayed after an ambush by the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Despot" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Despot">Serbian Despot</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Durad_Brankovic" class="mw-redirect" title="Durad Brankovic">Durad Brankovic</a><sup id="cite_ref-Malcolm_2002_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malcolm_2002-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the late 19th century, it was the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_National_Awakening" title="Albanian National Awakening">Albanian National Awakening</a>. Following their defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a>, the Ottomans <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1913)" title="Treaty of London (1913)">ceded</a> Kosovo to Serbia and Montenegro. Both countries joined <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and following a period of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavism" title="Yugoslavism">Yugoslav unitarianism</a> in the Kingdom, the post-World War II <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslav</a> constitution established the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo" title="Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija</a> within the Yugoslav constituent republic of Serbia. Tensions between Kosovo's Albanian and Serb communities simmered through the 20th century and occasionally erupted into major violence, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a> of 1998 and 1999, which resulted in the withdrawal of the Yugoslav army, the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Administration_Mission_in_Kosovo" title="United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo">United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo</a> and the declaration of independence in 2008. Serbia does not recognize Kosovo as a sovereign state, although with the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">2013 Brussels Agreement</a>, it has accepted its state institutions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="previously supported by a personal blog post, which is not a reliable source (January 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> While Serbia recognises administration of the territory by Kosovo's elected government, it continues to claim it as the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kosovo has an upper-middle-income <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kosovo" title="Economy of Kosovo">economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_category_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy_category-19">[19]</a></sup> It has experienced solid <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_Kosovo" title="International rankings of Kosovo">economic growth</a> over the last decade by international financial institutions, and growth every year since the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">financial crisis of 2007–2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_category_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy_category-19">[19]</a></sup> Kosovo is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, and has applied for membership of <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a> and for observer status in the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_the_Islamic_Cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation of the Islamic Cooperation">Organization of the Islamic Cooperation</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Kosovo" title="Names of Kosovo">Names of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Illyria_and_Dardania_Kingdoms.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Illyria_and_Dardania_Kingdoms.png/220px-Illyria_and_Dardania_Kingdoms.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Illyria_and_Dardania_Kingdoms.png/330px-Illyria_and_Dardania_Kingdoms.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Illyria_and_Dardania_Kingdoms.png/440px-Illyria_and_Dardania_Kingdoms.png 2x" data-file-width="1596" data-file-height="1576"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Illyria_and_Dardania_Kingdoms.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dardania" title="Kingdom of Dardania">Dardania</a> in the 4th century during the sovereignty of the Roman Empire.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The entire region that today corresponds to the territory is commonly referred to in English simply as <i>Kosovo</i> and in <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> as <i>Kosova</i> (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_grammar" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian grammar">definite form</a>, <small>Albanian pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[kɔˈsɔːva]</a></span>) or <i><i lang="sq" title="Albanian-language text">Kosovë</i></i> ("indefinite" form, <small>Albanian pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[kɔˈsɔːv]</a></span>). In Serbia, a formal distinction is made between the eastern and western areas; the term <i><i lang="sr-Latn" title="Serbian-language text">Kosovo</i></i> (<span lang="sr" title="Serbian-language text">Косово</span>) is used for the eastern part centred on the historical <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_field_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo field (region)">Kosovo Field</a>, while the western part is called <i><a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a></i> (<span lang="sr" title="Serbian-language text">Метохија</span>) (known as <i>Dukagjini</i> in Albanian).<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-serbia_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-serbia-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><i>Kosovo</i> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sr-Cyrl">Косово</span>, <small>Serbo-Croatian pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">[kôsoʋo]</a></span>) is the Serbian neuter <a href="/wiki/Possessive_adjective" class="mw-redirect" title="Possessive adjective">possessive adjective</a> of <i>kos</i> (кос) "<a href="/wiki/Common_blackbird" title="Common blackbird">blackbird</a>", an <a href="/wiki/Ellipsis_(linguistics)" title="Ellipsis (linguistics)">ellipsis</a> for <i>Kosovo Polje</i>, 'blackbird field', the name of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_field_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo field (region)">a plain</a> situated in the eastern half of today's Kosovo and the site of the 1389 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Inc.2015_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inc.2015-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The name of the plain was applied to <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Province,_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Province, Ottoman Empire">the Kosovo Province</a> created in 1864. </p>
      <p>Albanians also refer to Kosovo as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dardania" title="Kingdom of Dardania">Dardania</a>, the name of an ancient kingdom and later <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Roman province</a>, which covered the territory of modern-day Kosovo. The name is derived from the ancient tribe of the <a href="/wiki/Dardani" title="Dardani">Dardani</a>, possibly related to a Proto-Albanian word <i>dardā</i>, which means "pear".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The former Kosovo President <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Rugova" title="Ibrahim Rugova">Ibrahim Rugova</a> had been an enthusiastic backer of a "Dardanian" identity and the Kosovan flag and presidential seal refer to this national identity. However, the name "Kosova" remains more widely used among the Albanian population. </p>
      <p>The current borders of Kosovo were drawn while part of Yugoslavia in 1945, when the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija_(1945%E2%80%931963)" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Region of Kosovo and Metohija (1945–1963)">Autonomous Region of Kosovo and Metohija (1945–1963)</a> was created as an administrative division of the new <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of Serbia">People's Republic of Serbia</a>. In 1963, it was raised from the level of an autonomous region to the level of an autonomous province as the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija_(1963%E2%80%931968)" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija (1963–1968)">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija (1963–1968)</a>. In 1968, the dual name "Kosovo and Metohija" was reduced to a simple "Kosovo" in the name of the <i>Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo</i>. In 1990, the province was renamed the <i>Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The official conventional long name of the state is <i>Republic of Kosovo</i>, as defined by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kosovo" title="Constitution of Kosovo">Constitution of Kosovo</a>, and is used to represent Kosovo internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Additionally, as a result of an <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">arrangement agreed between Pristina and Belgrade</a> in talks mediated by the European Union, Kosovo has participated in some international forums and organisations under the title "Kosovo*" with a footnote stating "This designation is without prejudice to positions on status, and is in line with UNSC 1244 and the ICJ Opinion on the Kosovo declaration of independence". This arrangement, which has been dubbed the "asterisk agreement", was agreed in an 11-point arrangement agreed on 24 February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kosovo" title="History of Kosovo">History of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_development">Early development</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Archaeology_of_Kosovo" title="Archaeology of Kosovo">Archaeology of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Dardania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hyjnesha_muze.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hyjnesha_muze.jpg/220px-Hyjnesha_muze.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hyjnesha_muze.jpg/330px-Hyjnesha_muze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hyjnesha_muze.jpg/440px-Hyjnesha_muze.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hyjnesha_muze.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Goddess_on_the_Throne" title="Goddess on the Throne">Goddess on the Throne</a> is one of the most significant archaeological artifacts of Kosovo and has been adopted as the symbol of <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The strategic position including the abundant natural resources were favorable for the development of human settlements in Kosovo, as is highlighted by the hundreds of archaeological sites identified throughout its territory. The first archaeological expedition in Kosovo was organized by the Austro-Hungarian army during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Tumuli" class="mw-redirect" title="Tumuli">tumuli</a> burial grounds of Nepërbishti within the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Prizren" title="District of Prizren">district of Prizren</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SchermerShukriu_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchermerShukriu-27">[27]</a></sup> Since 2000, the increase in archaeological expeditions has revealed many, previously unknown sites. The earliest documented traces in Kosovo are associated to the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a>, namely there are indications that cave dwellings might have existed, as for instance the Radivojce Cav close the spring of the <a href="/wiki/Drin_(river)" title="Drin (river)">Drin River</a>, then there are some indications at Grnčar Cave in the <a href="/wiki/Vitina_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vitina (town)">municipality of Vitina</a> and the Dema and Karamakaz Caves in <a href="/wiki/Peja" title="Peja">municipality of Peja</a> and others. </p>
      <p>Human settlement during the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> has not yet been confirmed by archaeological expeditions. The earliest archaeological evidence of organized settlement, which have been found in Kosovo, belong to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Star%C4%8Devo_culture" title="Starčevo culture">Starčevo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da_culture" title="Vinča culture">Vinča</a> cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-Berisha_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berisha-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vlashnj%C3%AB" title="Vlashnjë">Vlashnjë</a> and <a href="/wiki/Runik" title="Runik">Runik</a> are important sites of the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_sites_in_Kosovo" title="Neolithic sites in Kosovo">Neolithic era</a>. The rock art paintings at Mrrizi i Kobajës, near <a href="/wiki/Vlashnj%C3%AB" title="Vlashnjë">Vlashnjë</a> are the first find of prehistoric art in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Amongs the finds of excavations in Neolithic Runik is a baked-clay <a href="/wiki/Ocarina" title="Ocarina">ocarina</a>, which is the first musical instrument to ever be recorded in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-Berisha_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berisha-28">[28]</a></sup> The beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_Europe" title="Bronze Age Europe">Bronze Age</a> coincides with the presence of <a href="/wiki/Tumuli" class="mw-redirect" title="Tumuli">tumuli</a> burial grounds in western Kosovo as in the site of <a href="/wiki/Romaj%C3%AB" title="Romajë">Romajë</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SchermerShukriu_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchermerShukriu-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Therefore, until arguments of Paleolithic and Mesolithic man are confirmed, Neolithic man, respectively the Neolithic sites are considered as the chronological beginning of population in Kosovo. From this period until today Kosovo has been inhabited, and traces of activities of societies from prehistoric, ancient and up to medieval time are visible throughout its territory. Whereas, in some archaeological sites, multilayer settlements clearly reflect the continuity of life through centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg/220px-ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg/330px-ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg/440px-ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2467"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ruins of Ancient <a href="/wiki/Ulpiana" title="Ulpiana">Ulpiana</a> situated south-east of <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>. The city played an important role in the development of one of the most important cities in the Roman province of Dardania.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Dardani" title="Dardani">Dardani</a> were the most important <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Balkan_languages" title="Paleo-Balkan languages">Paleo-Balkan</a> tribe in the region of Kosovo. A wide area which consists of Kosovo, parts of Northern Macedonia and eastern Serbia was named <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dardania" title="Kingdom of Dardania">Dardania</a> after them in classical antiquity. The eastern parts of the region were at the <a href="/wiki/Thraco-Illyrian" title="Thraco-Illyrian">Thraco-Illyrian</a> contact zone. In archaeological research, Illyrian names are predominant in western Dardania (present-day Kosovo), while Thracian names are mostly found in eastern Dardania (present-day south-eastern Serbia). </p>
      <p>Thracian names are absent in western Dardania; some Illyrian names appear in the eastern parts. Thus, their identification as either an <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> tribe has been a subject of debate; the ethnolinguistic relationship between the two groups being largely uncertain and debated itself as well. The correspondence of Illyrian names - including those of the ruling elite - in Dardania with those of the southern Illyrians suggests a "thracianization" of parts of Dardania.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The Dardani retained an individuality and succeeded to maintain themselves as a community after Roman conquest and they played an important role in the formation of new groupings in the Roman era.<sup id="cite_ref-Papazoglou_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Papazoglou-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Roman state annexed Dardania by the first century CE. The importance of the area lay in its mining potential (<i>metalla Dardana</i>) which was heavily exploited in the CE centuries as highlighted by the large mining complex of <a href="/wiki/Municipium_Dardanorum" title="Municipium Dardanorum">Municipium Dardanorum</a> and the designation of part of the region as an imperial mining district. Kosovo was part of two provinces, <a href="/wiki/Praevalitana" title="Praevalitana">Praevalitana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Dardania</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ulpiana" title="Ulpiana">Ulpiana</a> is the most important <a href="/wiki/Municipium" title="Municipium">municipium</a> which developed in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETeichner201581_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETeichner201581-33">[33]</a></sup> It was refounded as <i>Justiniana Secunda</i> under <a href="/wiki/Justinian" class="mw-redirect" title="Justinian">Justinian</a> in the 6th century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETeichner201583_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETeichner201583-34">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span></h3> 
      <table class="box-POV plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-POV" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" decoding="async" width="45" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="354">
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           The <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutrality</a> of this section is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">disputed</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Kosovo##" title="Talk:Kosovo">talk page</a>.           </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:248px;max-width:248px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:122px;max-width:122px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Basilios_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Basilios_II.jpg/120px-Basilios_II.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="149" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Basilios_II.jpg/180px-Basilios_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Basilios_II.jpg/240px-Basilios_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="894"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:122px;max-width:122px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Stefan_the_First-Crowned,_fresco_from_Mile%C5%A1eva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Stefan_the_First-Crowned%2C_fresco_from_Mile%C5%A1eva.jpg/120px-Stefan_the_First-Crowned%2C_fresco_from_Mile%C5%A1eva.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="184" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Stefan_the_First-Crowned%2C_fresco_from_Mile%C5%A1eva.jpg/180px-Stefan_the_First-Crowned%2C_fresco_from_Mile%C5%A1eva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Stefan_the_First-Crowned%2C_fresco_from_Mile%C5%A1eva.jpg/240px-Stefan_the_First-Crowned%2C_fresco_from_Mile%C5%A1eva.jpg 2x" data-file-width="282" data-file-height="432"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <b>Left:</b> Eastern Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">Basil II</a>, regained Kosovo from the Bulgarian Empire 
          <br><b>Right:</b> Serbian King, <a href="/wiki/Stefan_the_First-Crowned" title="Stefan the First-Crowned">Stefan Nemanjić</a> ended Byzantine rule in the 13th century
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><br> </p>
      <p>In the next centuries, Kosovo was a frontier province of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>. The region was exposed to an increasing number of raids from the 4th century AD onward, culminating with the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_migrations" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic migrations">Slavic migrations</a> of the 6th and 7th centuries. </p>
      <p>There is one intriguing line of argument to suggest that the Slav presence in Kosovo and southernmost part of the Morava valley may have been quite weak in the first one or two centuries of Slav settlement. Only in the ninth century do we see the expansion of a strong Slav (or quasi-Slav) power into this region. Under a series of ambitious rulers, the Bulgarians - a Slav population which absorbed, linguistically and culturally, its ruling elite of Turkic Bulgars - pushed westwards across modern Macedonia and eastern Serbia, until by the 850's they had taken over Kosovo and were pressing on the border of Rasci.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a> acquired Kosovo by the mid 9th century, but Byzantine control was <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_conquest_of_Bulgaria" title="Byzantine conquest of Bulgaria">restored</a> by the late 10th century. In 1072, the leaders of the Bulgarian <a href="/wiki/Uprising_of_Georgi_Voiteh" class="mw-redirect" title="Uprising of Georgi Voiteh">Uprising of Georgi Voiteh</a> traveled from their center in <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a> to Prizren and held a meeting in which they invited <a href="/wiki/Mihailo_Vojislavljevi%C4%87" title="Mihailo Vojislavljević">Mihailo Vojislavljević</a> of <a href="/wiki/Duklja" title="Duklja">Duklja</a> to send them assistance. Mihailo sent his son, <a href="/wiki/Constantine_Bodin" title="Constantine Bodin">Constantine Bodin</a> with 300 of his soldiers. After they met, the Bulgarian magnates proclaimed him "Emperor of the Bulgarians".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The uprising was defeated by <a href="/wiki/Nikephoros_Bryennios_the_Elder" title="Nikephoros Bryennios the Elder">Nikephoros Bryennios</a>. <a href="/wiki/Demetrios_Chomatenos" title="Demetrios Chomatenos">Demetrios Chomatenos</a> is the last Byzantine archbishop of Ohrid to include Prizren in his jurisdiction until 1219.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Nemanja" title="Stefan Nemanja">Stefan Nemanja</a> had seized the area along the <a href="/wiki/White_Drin" title="White Drin">White Drin</a> in 1185-95 and the ecclesiastical split of Prizren from the Patriarchate in 1219 was the final act of establishing <a href="/wiki/Nemanji%C4%87_dynasty" title="Nemanjić dynasty">Nemanjić</a> rule. <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Jire%C4%8Dek" title="Konstantin Jireček">Konstantin Jireček</a> concluded, from the correspondence of archbishop Demetrios of Ohrid (1216–36), that western Kosovo, in particular the <a href="/wiki/Gjakova" title="Gjakova">Gjakova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> areas, was part of the northeasternmost area of Albanian settlement prior to the Slavic expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-Abulafia1999_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abulafia1999-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gracanica_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Gracanica_1.jpg/250px-Gracanica_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Gracanica_1.jpg/375px-Gracanica_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Gracanica_1.jpg/500px-Gracanica_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4280" data-file-height="2830"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gracanica_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Gra%C4%8Danica_Monastery" title="Gračanica Monastery">Gračanica Monastery</a> is <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage site">UNESCO World Heritage site</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The zenith of Serbian power was reached in 1346, with the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a>(1346-1371). During the 13th and 14th centuries, Kosovo became a political, cultural and religious centre of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(medieval)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (medieval)">Serbian Kingdom</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the late 13th century, the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Archbishopric</a> was moved to <a href="/wiki/Peja" title="Peja">Peja</a>, and rulers centred themselves between <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> during which time thousands of Christian monasteries and feudal-style forts and castles were erected.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Du%C5%A1an" title="Stefan Dušan">Stefan Dušan</a> used <a href="/wiki/Prizren_Fortress" title="Prizren Fortress">Prizren Fortress</a> as one of his temporary courts for a time. When the Serbian Empire fragmented into a conglomeration of principalities in 1371, Kosovo became the hereditary land of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Brankovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Branković">House of Branković</a>. In the late 14th and the 15th centuries parts of Kosovo, the easternmost area of which was located near Pristina, were part of the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Dukagjini" title="Principality of Dukagjini">Principality of Dukagjini</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, which was later incorporated into an anti-Ottoman federation of all Albanian principalities, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Lezh%C3%AB" title="League of Lezhë">League of Lezhë</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sellers2010_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sellers2010-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Medieval_Monuments_in_Kosovo" title="Medieval Monuments in Kosovo">Medieval Monuments in Kosovo</a> is a today combined <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> consisting of four Serbian Orthodox churches and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Serbian_Orthodox_monasteries" title="List of Serbian Orthodox monasteries">monasteries</a>. The constructions were founded by members of <a href="/wiki/Nemanji%C4%87_dynasty" title="Nemanjić dynasty">Nemanjić dynasty</a>, the most important dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="Serbia in the Middle Ages">Serbia in the Middle Ages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_rule">Ottoman rule</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ottoman_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Ottoman Kosovo">History of Ottoman Kosovo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vilayet_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilayet of Kosovo">Vilayet of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 1389 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo</a>, Ottoman forces defeated a coalition led by <a href="/wiki/Lazar_of_Serbia" title="Lazar of Serbia">Lazar of Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jelavich1983_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jelavich1983-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prospect-magazine.co.uk_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prospect-magazine.co.uk-44">[44]</a></sup> Some historians, most notably <a href="/wiki/Noel_Malcolm" title="Noel Malcolm">Noel Malcolm</a>, argue that the battle of Kosovo in 1389 did not end with an Ottoman victory and "Serbian statehood did survive for another seventy years."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Soon after, Lazar's son accepted Turkish nominal vassalage (as did some other Serbian principalities) and Lazar's daughter was married to the Sultan to seal the peace. By 1459, Ottomans conquered the new Serbian capital of Smederevo,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> leaving <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> under <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungarian</a> rule until second quarter of the 16th century. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Serbian_Despotate_(1422)-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg/170px-Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg/255px-Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg/340px-Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="943" data-file-height="844"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Serbian_Despotate_(1422)-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bosnia" title="Kingdom of Bosnia">Kingdom of Bosnia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Despotate_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Despotate of Serbia">Despotate of Serbia</a> in 1422
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kosovo was part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> from 1455 to 1912, at first as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Subdivisions of the Ottoman Empire">eyalet</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a>, and from 1864 as a separate <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Province,_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Province, Ottoman Empire">province</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Vilayet" title="Vilayet">vilayet</a></i>). During this time, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> was introduced to the population. The <a href="/wiki/Vilayet_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilayet of Kosovo">Vilayet of Kosovo</a> was an area much larger than today's Kosovo; it included all today's Kosovo territory, sections of the <a href="/wiki/Sand%C5%BEak" title="Sandžak">Sandžak</a> region cutting into present-day <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0umadija_and_Western_Serbia" title="Šumadija and Western Serbia">Šumadija and Western Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> along with the <a href="/wiki/Kuk%C3%ABs" title="Kukës">Kukës</a> municipality, the surrounding region in present-day northern <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and also parts of north-western North Macedonia with the city of <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a> (then Üsküp), as its capital. Between 1881 and 1912 (its final phase), it was internally expanded to include other regions of present-day North Macedonia, including larger urban settlements such as <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0tip" title="Štip">Štip</a> (<i>İştip</i>), <a href="/wiki/Kumanovo" title="Kumanovo">Kumanovo</a> (<i>Kumanova</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Kratovo,_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Kratovo, Macedonia">Kratovo</a> (<i>Kratova</i>). According to some historians, Serbs likely formed a majority of Kosovo from the 8th to the mid-19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanac42_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanac42-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Nevertheless, this claim is difficult to prove, as historians who base their works on Ottoman sources of the time give solid evidence that at least the western and central parts of Kosovo had an Albanian majority. The scholar Fredrick F. Anscombe shows that Prizren and <a href="/wiki/Vu%C4%8Ditrn" title="Vučitrn">Vučitrn</a> (<i>Vulçitrin</i>) had no Serbian population in early 17th century. Prizren was inhabited by a mix of Catholic and Muslim Albanians, while Vučitrn had a mix of Albanian and Turkish speakers, followed by tiny a Serbian minority. <a href="/wiki/Gjakova" title="Gjakova">Gjakova</a> was founded by Albanians in the 16th century, and <a href="/wiki/Peja" title="Peja">Peja</a> (<i>İpek</i>) had a continuous presence of the Albanian Kelmendi tribe. Central Kosovo was mixed, but large parts of the <a href="/wiki/Drenica" title="Drenica">Drenica Valley</a> were ethnically Albanian. Central Kosovo, as well as the cities of Prizren, Gjakova, and the region of <a href="/wiki/Has_(region)" title="Has (region)">Has</a> regularly supplied the Ottoman forces with levies and mercenaries.<sup id="cite_ref-Anscombe_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anscombe-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early sixteenth century, a large migration of Albanians into Kosovo resulted in a sizeable ethnic Albanian presence in some parts of Western Kosovo which continued into the next century.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohen_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-50">[50]</a></sup>Historian <a href="/wiki/Noel_Malcolm" title="Noel Malcolm">Noel Malcolm</a> challenges this view, using Ottoman documents that recorded migrants coming into the Kosovo region from the 15th to the 18th century and Albanian Catholic sources from the 17th century of northern Albania which recorded migrations out of the region, Malcolm argues majority of the migrants into the Kosovo region during this period were not Albanian.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The population of Kosovo was also much bigger than that of northern and central Albania and its rate of growth lower.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Kosovo was part of the wider Ottoman region to be occupied by Austrian forces during the Great War of 1683–99,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> but the Ottomans re-established their rule of the region. Such acts of assistance by the Austrian Empire (then arch-rivals of the Ottoman Empire), or Russia, were always abortive or temporary at best.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanac42_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanac42-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In 1690, the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Patriarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Patriarch">Serbian Patriarch</a> <a href="/wiki/Arsenije_III_%C4%8Carnojevi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Arsenije III Čarnojević">Arsenije III</a> led thousands people from Kosovo to the Christian north, in what came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Serb_Migration" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Serb Migration">Great Serb Migration</a>. Anscombe casts doubt on the fact that this exodus affected Kosovo, since there is no evidence that parts of Kosovo were depopulated. Evidence of depopulation can only be found in areas between <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="Niš">Niš</a> and Belgrade. Some Albanians from Skopje and other regions were displaced in order to fill some areas around Niš, but there is no evidence that such events took place in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In 1766, the Ottomans abolished the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Patriarchate_of_Pe%C4%87" title="Serbian Patriarchate of Peć">Patriarchate of Peja</a> and fully imposed the <i><a href="/wiki/Jizya" title="Jizya">jizya</a></i> on its non-Muslim population. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg/220px-Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg/330px-Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg/440px-Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4528" data-file-height="3200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The city of <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> was the cultural and intellectual centre of Kosovo during the Ottoman period in the Middle Ages and is now the historic capital of Kosovo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although initially stout opponents of the advancing Turks, Albanian chiefs ultimately came to accept the Ottomans as sovereigns. The resulting alliance facilitated the mass conversion of Albanians to Islam. Given that the Ottoman Empire's subjects were divided along religious (rather than ethnic) lines, Islamisation greatly elevated the status of Albanian chiefs. Prior to this, they were organised along simple tribal lines, living in the mountainous areas of modern Albania (from Kruje to the Šar range).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Soon, they expanded into a depopulated Kosovo,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> as well as northwestern Macedonia, although some might have been autochthonous to the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanac46_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanac46-59">[59]</a></sup> However, Banac favours the idea that the main settlers of the time were Vlachs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanac42_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanac42-47">[47]</a></sup> Centuries earlier, Albanians of Kosovo were predominantly Christian and Albanians and Serbs for the most part co-existed peacefully. The Ottomans appeared to have a more deliberate approach to converting the Roman Catholic population of whom were mostly Albanians as compared to adherents of Eastern Orthodoxy who were mostly Serbs, as they viewed the former less favorably due to its allegiance to Rome, a competing regional power.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohen_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many Albanians gained prominent positions in the Ottoman government. "Albanians had little cause of unrest", according to author Dennis Hupchik. "If anything, they grew important in Ottoman internal affairs."<sup id="cite_ref-hupchik_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hupchik-60">[60]</a></sup> In the 19th century, there was an <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_under_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Rise of nationalism under the Ottoman Empire">awakening</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_nationalism" title="Ethnic nationalism">ethnic nationalism</a> throughout the Balkans. The underlying ethnic tensions became part of a broader struggle of Christian Serbs against Muslim Albanians.<sup id="cite_ref-prospect-magazine.co.uk_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prospect-magazine.co.uk-44">[44]</a></sup> The ethnic <a href="/wiki/National_Renaissance_of_Albania" class="mw-redirect" title="National Renaissance of Albania">Albanian nationalism</a> movement was centred in Kosovo. In 1878 the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Prizren" title="League of Prizren">League of Prizren</a> (<i lang="sq" title="Albanian-language text">Lidhja e Prizrenit</i>) was formed. This was a political organisation that sought to unify all the Albanians of the Ottoman Empire in a common struggle for autonomy and greater cultural rights,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> although they generally desired the continuation of the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The League was dis-established in 1881 but enabled the awakening of a <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">national identity</a> among Albanians.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Albanian ambitions competed with those of the Serbs. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a> wished to incorporate this land that had formerly been within its empire. </p>
      <p>The modern Albanian-Serbian conflict has its roots in the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Albanians_1877%E2%80%931878" class="mw-redirect" title="Expulsion of the Albanians 1877–1878">expulsion of the Albanians in 1877–1878 from areas that became incorporated into the</a> <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia" title="Principality of Serbia">Principality of Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> During and after the <a href="/wiki/Serbian%E2%80%93Ottoman_War_(1876%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian–Ottoman War (1876–78)">Serbian–Ottoman War</a> of 1876–78, between 30,000 and 70,000 Muslims, mostly Albanians, were expelled by the <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces_of_the_Principality_of_Serbia" title="Armed forces of the Principality of Serbia">Serb army</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Ni%C5%A1" title="Sanjak of Niš">Sanjak of Niš</a> and fled to the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Vilayet" title="Kosovo Vilayet">Kosovo Vilayet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Batakovic1992_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Batakovic1992-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Elsie2010_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsie2010-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> According to Austrian data, by the 1890s Kosovo was 70% Muslim (nearly entirely of Albanian descent) and less than 30% non-Muslim (primarily Serbs).<sup id="cite_ref-Cohen_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-50">[50]</a></sup> At the turn of the century in 1901, widespread <a href="/wiki/1901_massacres_of_Serbs" title="1901 massacres of Serbs">massacres</a> were committed against the Serbian population by the Albanian population across the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Vilayet" title="Kosovo Vilayet">Kosovo Vilayet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-King-Mason-30_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-King-Mason-30-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Turk">Young Turk</a> movement took control of the Ottoman Empire after a coup in 1912 which deposed Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II" title="Abdul Hamid II">Abdul Hamid&nbsp;II</a>. The movement supported a centralised form of government and opposed any sort of autonomy desired by the various nationalities of the Ottoman Empire. An allegiance to <a href="/wiki/Ottomanism" title="Ottomanism">Ottomanism</a> was promoted instead.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> An Albanian uprising in 1912 exposed the empire's northern territories in Kosovo and <a href="/wiki/Novi_Pazar" title="Novi Pazar">Novi Pazar</a>, which led to an invasion by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Kingdom of Montenegro</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Dynasty">The Ottomans</a> suffered a serious defeat at the hands of Albanians in 1912, culminating in the Ottoman loss of most of its Albanian-inhabited lands. The Albanians threatened to march all the way to <a href="/wiki/Salonika" class="mw-redirect" title="Salonika">Salonika</a> and reimpose Abdul Hamid.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Serbia1913.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Serbia1913.png/220px-Serbia1913.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Serbia1913.png/330px-Serbia1913.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Serbia1913.png/440px-Serbia1913.png 2x" data-file-width="663" data-file-height="912"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Serbia1913.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Division of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_vilayet" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo vilayet">Kosovo vilayet</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a> (<i>yellow</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Kingdom of Montenegro</a> (<i>green</i>) following the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> 1913.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A wave of Albanians in the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Military of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman army</a> ranks also deserted during this period, refusing to fight their own kin. In September 1912, a joint Balkan force made up of Serbian, Montenegrin, Bulgarian and Greek forces drove the Ottomans out of most of their European possessions. The rise of nationalism hampered relations between Albanians and <a href="/wiki/Serbs_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbs in Kosovo">Serbs in Kosovo</a>, due to influence from Russians, Austrians and Ottomans.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> After the Ottomans' defeat in the <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">First Balkan War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1913)" title="Treaty of London (1913)">1913 Treaty of London</a> was signed with <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Western Kosovo (Metohija)</a> ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Kingdom of Montenegro</a> and Eastern Kosovo ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Soon, there were concerted Serbian colonisation efforts in Kosovo during various periods between Serbia's 1912 takeover of the province and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War&nbsp;II</a>. So the population of Serbs in Kosovo fell after World War&nbsp;II, but it had increased considerably before then.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An exodus of the local Albanian population occurred. Serbian authorities promoted creating new Serb settlements in Kosovo as well as the assimilation of Albanians into Serbian society.<sup id="cite_ref-Schabnel_2001_20_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schabnel_2001_20-78">[78]</a></sup> Numerous colonist Serb families moved into Kosovo, equalising the demographic balance between Albanians and Serbs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg/190px-Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg/285px-Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg/380px-Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="776" data-file-height="1050"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>German soldiers set fire to a Serbian village near <a href="/wiki/Mitrovica,_Kosovo" title="Mitrovica, Kosovo">Mitrovica</a>, circa 1941.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the winter of 1915–16, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Kosovo saw the retreat of the Serbian army as Kosovo was occupied by <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria%E2%80%93Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Austria–Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>. In 1918, the Allied Powers pushed the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> out of Kosovo. After the end of World War I, the Kingdom of Serbia was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenians</a> on 1 December 1918. </p>
      <p>Kosovo was split into four counties, three being a part of Serbia (<a href="/wiki/Zve%C4%8Dan" title="Zvečan">Zvečan</a>, Kosovo and southern <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a>) and one of Montenegro (northern Metohija). However, the new administration system since 26 April 1922 split Kosovo among three districts (<a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblast</a>) of the Kingdom: Kosovo, Raška and Zeta. In 1929, the country was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a> and the territories of Kosovo were reorganised among the <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Banovina" title="Zeta Banovina">Banate of Zeta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Morava_Banovina" title="Morava Banovina">Banate of Morava</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vardar_Banovina" title="Vardar Banovina">Banate of Vardar</a>. In order to change the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kosovo" title="Demographics of Kosovo">ethnic composition of Kosovo</a>, between 1912 and 1941 a <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonisation of Kosovo">large-scale Serbian re-colonisation of Kosovo</a> was undertaken by the Belgrade government. Meanwhile, Kosovar Albanians' right to receive education in their own language was denied alongside other non-Slavic or unrecognised Slavic nations of Yugoslavia, as the kingdom only recognised the Slavic Croat, Serb, and Slovene nations as constituent nations of Yugoslavia, while other Slavs had to identify as one of the three official Slavic nations while non-Slav nations were only deemed as minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-Schabnel_2001_20_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schabnel_2001_20-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Albanians and other <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> were forced to emigrate, mainly with the land reform which struck Albanian landowners in 1919, but also with direct violent measures.<sup id="cite_ref-daskalovski_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daskalovski-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-malcolm_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malcolm-80">[80]</a></sup> In 1935 and 1938 two agreements between the Kingdom of Yugoslavia and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> were signed on the expatriation of 240,000 Albanians to Turkey, which was not completed because of the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Axis_invasion_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis invasion of Yugoslavia">Axis invasion of Yugoslavia</a> in 1941, most of Kosovo was assigned to Italian-controlled Albania, with the rest being controlled by Germany and Bulgaria. A three-dimensional conflict ensued, involving inter-ethnic, ideological, and international affiliations, with the first being most important. Nonetheless, these conflicts were relatively low-level compared with other areas of Yugoslavia during the war years, with one Serb historian estimating that 3,000 Albanians and 4,000 Serbs and Montenegrins were killed, and two others estimating war dead at 12,000 Albanians and 10,000 Serbs and Montenegrins.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> An official investigation conducted by the Yugoslav government in 1964 recorded nearly 8,000 war-related fatalities in Kosovo between 1941 and 1945, 5,489 of whom were Serb and Montenegrin and 2,177 of whom were Albanian.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> It is not disputed that between 1941 and 1945 tens of thousands of Serbs, mostly recent colonists, fled from Kosovo. Estimates range from 30,000 to 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> There had been large-scale Albanian immigration from Albania to Kosovo which is by some scholars estimated in the range from 72,000<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERamet2006141_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERamet2006141-86">[86]</a></sup> to 260,000 people (with a tendency to escalate, the last figure being in a petition of 1985). Some historians and contemporary references emphasise that a large-scale migration of Albanians from Albania to Kosovo is not recorded in Axis documents.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communist_Yugoslavia">Communist Yugoslavia</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo" title="Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo">Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg/240px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg.png" decoding="async" width="240" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg/360px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg/480px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The flag of the Albanian Minority of Kosovo in the Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The province as in its outline today first took shape in 1945 as the <i>Autonomous Kosovo-Metohian Area</i>. Until World War II, the only entity bearing the name of Kosovo had been a political unit carved from the former <a href="/wiki/Vilayet" title="Vilayet">vilayet</a> which bore no special significance to its internal population. In the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> (which previously controlled the territory), it had been a vilayet with its borders having been revised on several occasions. When the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Province,_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Province, Ottoman Empire">Ottoman province</a> had last existed, it included areas which were by now either ceded to <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, or found themselves within the newly created Yugoslav republics of <a href="/wiki/SR_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="SR Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, or <a href="/wiki/SR_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="SR Macedonia">Macedonia</a> (including its previous capital, <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>) with another part in the <a href="/wiki/Sand%C5%BEak" title="Sandžak">Sandžak</a> region of southwest Serbia. </p>
      <p>Tensions between ethnic Albanians and the Yugoslav government were significant, not only due to ethnic tensions but also due to political ideological concerns, especially regarding relations with neighbouring Albania.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-88">[88]</a></sup> Harsh repressive measures were imposed on Kosovo Albanians due to suspicions that there were sympathisers of the <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinist</a> regime of <a href="/wiki/Enver_Hoxha" title="Enver Hoxha">Enver Hoxha</a> of Albania.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-88">[88]</a></sup> In 1956, a show trial in Pristina was held in which multiple Albanian Communists of Kosovo were convicted of being infiltrators from Albania and were given long prison sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-88">[88]</a></sup> High-ranking Serbian communist official <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Rankovi%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Ranković">Aleksandar Ranković</a> sought to secure the position of the Serbs in Kosovo and gave them dominance in Kosovo's <a href="/wiki/Nomenklatura" title="Nomenklatura">nomenklatura</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fadil_Hoxha,_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg/220px-Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg/330px-Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg/440px-Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1362" data-file-height="1802"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fadil_Hoxha,_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Fadil_Hoxha" title="Fadil Hoxha">Fadil Hoxha</a>, the Vice-President of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>, from 1978 to 1979
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> in Kosovo at this time was repressed and both Albanians and Muslim Slavs were encouraged to declare themselves to be Turkish and emigrate to Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_88-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-88">[88]</a></sup> At the same time Serbs and Montenegrins dominated the government, security forces, and industrial employment in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_88-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-88">[88]</a></sup> Albanians resented these conditions and protested against them in the late 1960s, accusing the actions taken by authorities in Kosovo as being colonialist, as well as demanding that Kosovo be made a republic, or declaring support for Albania.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_88-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-88">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the ouster of Ranković in 1966, the agenda of pro-decentralisation reformers in Yugoslavia, especially from Slovenia and Croatia, succeeded in the late 1960s in attaining substantial decentralisation of powers, creating substantial autonomy in Kosovo and Vojvodina, and recognising a <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Muslim Yugoslav</a> nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296-90">[90]</a></sup> As a result of these reforms, there was a massive overhaul of Kosovo's nomenklatura and police, that shifted from being Serb-dominated to ethnic Albanian-dominated through firing Serbs in large scale.<sup id="cite_ref-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296-90">[90]</a></sup> Further concessions were made to the ethnic Albanians of Kosovo in response to unrest, including the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Universiteti_i_Prishtin%C3%ABs" class="mw-redirect" title="Universiteti i Prishtinës">University of Pristina</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian language</a> institution.<sup id="cite_ref-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296-90">[90]</a></sup> These changes created widespread fear among Serbs that they were being made <a href="/wiki/Second-class_citizen" title="Second-class citizen">second-class citizens</a> in Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> By the 1974 Constitution of Yugoslavia, Kosovo was granted major autonomy, allowing it to have its own administration, assembly, and judiciary; as well as having a membership in the collective presidency and the Yugoslav parliament, in which it held veto power.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg/240px-SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="240" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg/360px-SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg/480px-SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="431"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Republics and provinces of the SFR Yugoslavia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
