      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Kosovo" title="Geography of Kosovo">Geography of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Paradise_Lost.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Paradise_Lost.jpg/220px-Paradise_Lost.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Paradise_Lost.jpg/330px-Paradise_Lost.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Paradise_Lost.jpg/440px-Paradise_Lost.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="1440"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Paradise_Lost.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Landscape in <a href="/wiki/Rugova_(region)" title="Rugova (region)">Rugova</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Bjeshk%C3%ABt_e_Nemuna_National_Park" title="Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park">Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park</a> bordering <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Defined in a total area of 10,887 square kilometres (4,203 square miles), Kosovo is landlocked and located in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42°</a> and <a href="/wiki/43rd_parallel_north" title="43rd parallel north">43° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/20th_meridian_east" title="20th meridian east">20°</a> and <a href="/wiki/22nd_meridian_east" title="22nd meridian east">22° E</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> The northernmost point is Bellobërda at 43° 14' 06" northern latitude; the southernmost is Restelica at 41° 56' 40" northern latitude; the westernmost point is <a href="/wiki/Bog%C3%AB,_Kosovo" title="Bogë, Kosovo">Bogë</a> at 20° 3' 23" eastern longitude; and the easternmost point is <a href="/wiki/Desivojca" title="Desivojca">Desivojca</a> at 21° 44' 21" eastern longitude. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Velika_Rudoka" title="Velika Rudoka">Velika Rudoka</a> at 2,658 metres (8,720&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a>, and the lowest is the <a href="/wiki/White_Drin" title="White Drin">White Drin</a> at 297 metres (974&nbsp;ft). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Brod_Dragash.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Brod_Dragash.jpg/220px-Brod_Dragash.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Brod_Dragash.jpg/330px-Brod_Dragash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Brod_Dragash.jpg/440px-Brod_Dragash.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2394"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Brod_Dragash.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar Mountains</a> encompass one-tenth of Kosovo's territory.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most of the borders of Kosovo are dominated by mountainous and high terrain. The most noticeable <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topographical</a> features are the <a href="/wiki/Prokletije" title="Prokletije">Prokletije</a> and the <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar Mountains</a>. The Prokletije, are a geological continuation of the <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Dinaric Alps</a>. The mountains run laterally through the west along the border with <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>. The southeast is predominantly the Šar Mountains, which constitute the border with <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>. Besides the mountain ranges, Kosovo's territory consists mostly of two major plains, the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Plain">Kosovo Plain</a> in the east and the <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija Plain</a> in the west. </p>
      <p>Kosovo's hydrological resources are relatively small. The longest rivers of Kosovo include the <a href="/wiki/White_Drin" title="White Drin">White Drin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_Morava" title="South Morava">South Morava</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ibar_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibar River">Ibar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sitnica" title="Sitnica">Sitnica</a>, a tributary of Ibar, is the largest river lying completely within Kosovo's territory. River <a href="/wiki/Nerodimka_(river)" title="Nerodimka (river)">Nerodimka</a> represents Europe's only instance of a river bifurcation flowing into the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Kosovo" title="Climate of Kosovo">Climate of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg/220px-Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg/330px-Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg/440px-Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="1440"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">Alpine climate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pashallora" title="Pashallora">Pashallora</a> as seen from <a href="/wiki/Brezovica,_Kosovo" title="Brezovica, Kosovo">Brezovica</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most of Kosovo experiences predominantly a <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">Continental climate</a> with <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">Alpine</a> influences.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the climate is strongly influenced by Kosovo's proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> in the west, the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> in the south as well as the European continental landmass in the north.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The coldest areas is the mountainous region in the west and southeast, whereas an Alpine climate is prevalent. The warmest areas are mostly in the extreme southern areas close to the border with Albania, characterised by the Mediterranean climate. Mean monthly temperature ranges between 0&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (32&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>) (in January) and 22&nbsp;°C (72&nbsp;°F) (in July). Mean annual precipitation ranges from 600 to 1,300&nbsp;mm (24 to 51&nbsp;in) per year, and is well distributed year-round. </p>
      <p>To the northeast, the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Plain">Kosovo Plain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ibar_(river)" title="Ibar (river)">Ibar Valley</a> are drier with total precipitation of about 600 millimetres (24 inches) per year and more influenced by continental air masses, with colder winters and very hot summers. In the southwest, climatic area of <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a> receives more mediterranean influences with warmer summers, somewhat higher precipitation (700&nbsp;mm (28&nbsp;in)) and heavy snowfalls in the winter. The mountainous areas of <a href="/wiki/Prokletije" title="Prokletije">Prokletije</a> in the west, <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar Mountains</a> on the south and <a href="/wiki/Kopaonik" title="Kopaonik">Kopaonik</a> in the north experiences alpine climate, with high precipitation (900 to 1,300&nbsp;mm (35 to 51&nbsp;in) per year, short and fresh summers, and cold winters.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> The average annual temperature of Kosovo is 9.5&nbsp;°C (49.1&nbsp;°F). The warmest month is July with average temperature of 19.2&nbsp;°C (66.6&nbsp;°F), and the coldest is January with −1.3&nbsp;°C (29.7&nbsp;°F). Except <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istok" title="Istok">Istok</a>, all other meteorological stations in January recorded average temperatures under 0&nbsp;°C (32&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_of_Kosovo" title="Biodiversity of Kosovo">Biodiversity of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected areas of Kosovo">Protected areas of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_,_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_,_Rugove.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg/220px-Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg/330px-Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg/440px-Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4914" data-file-height="3255"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_,_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_,_Rugove.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bjeshk%C3%ABt_e_Nemuna_National_Park" title="Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park">Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park</a> is home to a wide range of flora and fauna species.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Located in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>, Kosovo receives floral and faunal species from Europe and <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>. Forests are widespread in Kosovo and cover at least 39% of the region. <a href="/wiki/Phytogeographically" class="mw-redirect" title="Phytogeographically">Phytogeographically</a>, it straddles the <a href="/wiki/Illyria" title="Illyria">Illyrian</a> province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. In addition, it falls within three terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Balkan_mixed_forests" title="Balkan mixed forests">Balkan mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Mountains_mixed_forests" title="Dinaric Mountains mixed forests">Dinaric Mountains mixed forests</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pindus_Mountains_mixed_forests" title="Pindus Mountains mixed forests">Pindus Mountains mixed forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-189">[189]</a></sup> Kosovo's biodiversity is conserved in two <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a>, eleven <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserves</a> and one hundred three other protected areas.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bjeshk%C3%ABt_e_Nemuna_National_Park" title="Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park">Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sharr_Mountains_National_Park" title="Sharr Mountains National Park">Sharr Mountains National Park</a> are the most important regions of vegetation and biodiversity in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-Maxhuni_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maxhuni-191">[191]</a></sup> Kosovo had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 5.19/10, ranking it 107<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-192">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">Flora</a> encompasses more than 1,800 species of <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plant" title="Vascular plant">vascular plant</a> species, but the actual number is estimated to be higher than 2,500 species.<sup id="cite_ref-KOSOVObio_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KOSOVObio-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> The diversity is the result of the complex interaction of geology and hydrology creating a wide variety of habitat conditions for flora growth. Although, Kosovo represents only 2.3% of the entire surface area of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, in terms of vegetation it has 25% of the Balkan flora and about 18% of the European flora.<sup id="cite_ref-KOSOVObio_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KOSOVObio-193">[193]</a></sup> The fauna is composed of a wide range of species.<sup id="cite_ref-Maxhuni_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maxhuni-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>14</span></sup> The mountainous west and southeast provide a great habitat for several <a href="/wiki/Rare_species" title="Rare species">rare</a> or <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a> species including <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lynx" title="Lynx">lynxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_cat" class="mw-redirect" title="Wild cat">wild cats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolve" class="mw-redirect" title="Wolve">wolves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox" title="Fox">foxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_goat" title="Wild goat">wild goats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roebucks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> A total of 255 species of <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a> have been recorded, with raptors such as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_imperial_eagle" title="Eastern imperial eagle">eastern imperial eagle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_kestrel" title="Lesser kestrel">lesser kestrel</a> living principally in the mountains of Kosovo. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kosovo" title="Demographics of Kosovo">Demographics of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Languages of Kosovo">Languages of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Population_of_Kosovo_(1921-2015).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png/220px-Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png/330px-Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png/440px-Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1502" data-file-height="846"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Population_of_Kosovo_(1921-2015).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The population of Kosovo from 1921 to 2015.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of Kosovo, as defined by <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Agency_of_Statistics" title="Kosovo Agency of Statistics">Agency of Statistics</a>, was estimated in 2011 to be approximately 1,740,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Chapter_1_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chapter_1-196">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> The overall <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy</a> at birth is 76.7 years; 74.1 years for males and 79.4 years for females.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Kosovo ranks <a href="/wiki/Balkans#Demographics" title="Balkans">11th most populous</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">149th</a> in the world. </p>
      <p>In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Institutions_of_Self-Government" title="Provisional Institutions of Self-Government">Provisional Institutions of Self Government</a> estimated the population of Kosovo to be between 1.9 and 2.2&nbsp;million with the <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> being the largest <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> followed by other groups such as <a href="/wiki/Bosniak_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosniak people">Bosniak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gorani_people" title="Gorani people">Gorani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> However, according to the 2009 <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a>, Kosovo's population stands at 1,804,838 persons. It stated that ethnic composition was 88% <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Albanians" title="Kosovo Albanians">Albanians</a>, 7% <a href="/wiki/Serbs_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbs of Kosovo">Serbs</a> and 5% of other ethnic groups including Bosniaks, Gorani, Roma, Turks, Ashkalis, Egyptians and <a href="/wiki/Janjevci" title="Janjevci">Janjevci&nbsp;– Croats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-200">[200]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Albanians, steadily increasing in number, may have constituted a majority in Kosovo since the 19th century, although the region's historical ethnic composition is disputed. Kosovo's political boundaries do not quite coincide with the ethnic boundary by which Albanians compose an absolute majority in every municipality; for example, Serbs form a local majority in <a href="/wiki/North_Kosovo" title="North Kosovo">North Kosovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Serb_enclaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Serb enclaves">two other municipalities</a>, while there are large areas with an Albanian majority outside of Kosovo, namely in the neighbouring regions of former Yugoslavia: the north-west of North Macedonia, and in the <a href="/wiki/Pre%C5%A1evo_Valley" title="Preševo Valley">Preševo Valley</a> in Southern Serbia. </p>
      <p>At 1.3% per year as of 2008 data, ethnic <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in Kosovo">Albanians in Kosovo</a> have the fastest rate of growth in population in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Over an 82-year period (1921–2003) the population of Kosovo grew to 460% of its original size. Whereas Albanians constituted 60% of Kosovo's 500,000 person population in 1931, by 1991 they reached 81% of Kosovo's 2 million person population.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> In the second half of the 20th century, Kosovo Albanians had three times higher birth rates than Serbs.<sup id="cite_ref-On_Genetic_Interests:_Family,_Ethnicity,_And_Humanity_in_an_Age_of_Mass_Migration_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-On_Genetic_Interests:_Family,_Ethnicity,_And_Humanity_in_an_Age_of_Mass_Migration-203">[203]</a></sup> In addition, most of Kosovo's pre-1999 <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Serbs" title="Kosovo Serbs">Serb</a> population relocated to Serbia proper following the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> campaign in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-Wills_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wills-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Kosovo" title="Municipalities of Kosovo">Municipalities of Kosovo</a> are largely rural, with only eight municipalities having more than 40,000 inhabitants living in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Kosovo" title="List of cities in Kosovo">urban areas</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> of Kosovo are <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> and the institutions are committed to ensure the equal use of both languages.<sup id="cite_ref-langauges_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-langauges-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Assessing_Minority_Language_Rights_in_Kosovo_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assessing_Minority_Language_Rights_in_Kosovo-205">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-COE-Municipalities_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COE-Municipalities-206">[206]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Roma</a> hold the status of official languages at municipal level if the linguistic community represents at least 5% of the total population of municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-langauges_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-langauges-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-COE-Municipalities_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COE-Municipalities-206">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Albanian is spoken as a <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a> by approximately 95% of the population, while Bosnian and Serbian are spoken by 1.7% and 1.6% of the population, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Due to the boycott of the census of North Kosovo, Bosnian resulted in being the second largest language after Albanian however, Serbian is <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> the second largest language in Kosovo. </p>
      <p>Although both Albanian and Serbian are official languages, municipal civil servants are only required to speak one of them in a professional setting and, according to Language Commissioner of Kosovo, Slaviša Mladenović, statement from 2015, no organisations have all of their documents in both languages.<sup id="cite_ref-ECMI-Kosovo_Language_Commissioner_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECMI-Kosovo_Language_Commissioner-208">[208]</a></sup> The Law on the Use of Languages gives <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> the status of an official language in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>, irrespective of the size of the <a href="/wiki/Turks_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks of Kosovo">Turkish community</a> living there.<sup id="cite_ref-COE-Municipalities_206-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COE-Municipalities-206">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A 2020 research report funded by the EU shows that there is a limited scale of trust and overall contact between the major ethnic groups in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Kosovo" title="Religion in Kosovo">Religion in Kosovo</a>
      </div>
