      </div> 
      <p>Kosovo is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> with no <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>; <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_belief" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of belief">freedom of belief</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_conscience" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of conscience">conscience</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">religion</a> is explicitly guaranteed in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kosovo" title="Constitution of Kosovo">Constitution of Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-163">[163]</a></sup> Kosovan society is strongly <a href="/wiki/Secularised" class="mw-redirect" title="Secularised">secularised</a> and is ranked first in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> and ninth in the world as free and equal for tolerance towards <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2011 census, 95.6% of the population of Kosovo was counted as <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> and 3.7% as <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> including 2.2% as <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> and 1.5% as <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_200-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-200">[200]</a></sup> The remaining 0.3% of the population reported having no religion, or another religion, or did not provide an adequate answer. Protestants, although recognised as a religious group in Kosovo by the government, were not represented in the census. The census was largely boycotted by the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Serbs" title="Kosovo Serbs">Kosovo Serbs</a> (who predominantly identify as <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Orthodox">Serbian Orthodox</a> Christians), especially in <a href="/wiki/North_Kosovo" title="North Kosovo">North Kosovo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> leaving the Serb population underrepresented.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Kosovo" title="Islam in Kosovo">Islam</a> is the most widely practiced religion in Kosovo and was first introduced in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a>. Today, Kosovo has the highest percentage of Muslims in Europe after <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> The majority of the Muslim population of Kosovo are ethnic <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Slavs" title="Muslim Slavs">Slavs</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Gorani_people" title="Gorani people">Gorani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Kosovo" title="Christianity in Kosovo">Christianity</a> has a long and continuous history in Kosovo which can be traced back to the <a href="/wiki/State_church_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="State church of the Roman Empire">Roman</a> invasion of the region. During the early and late Middle Ages, the entire <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a> had been <a href="/wiki/Christianised" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianised">Christianised</a> initially by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> and subsequently by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>. Followers of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> are predominantly Albanians with ethnic Serbs following the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>. In 2008, Protestant pastor Artur Krasniqi, primate of the Kosovo Protestant Evangelical Church, claimed that "as many as 15,000" Kosovar Albanians had converted to Protestantism since 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Relations between the Albanian Muslim and Albanian Roman Catholic communities in Kosovo are considered good, however both communities have few or no relations with the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox</a> community. In general, the Albanians define their <a href="/wiki/Ethnicity" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnicity">ethnicity</a> by <a href="/wiki/Language" title="***REMOVED***">language</a> and not by religion, while religion reflects a distinguishing identity feature among the Slavs of Kosovo and elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kosovo" title="Economy of Kosovo">Economy of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Industry_of_Kosovo" title="Industry of Kosovo">Industry of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kosovo-lignite.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kosovo-lignite.jpg/220px-Kosovo-lignite.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kosovo-lignite.jpg/330px-Kosovo-lignite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kosovo-lignite.jpg/440px-Kosovo-lignite.jpg 2x" data-file-width="467" data-file-height="345"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kosovo-lignite.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kosovo has the 5th largest <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a> reserves in the world.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kosovo" title="Economy of Kosovo">economy of Kosovo</a> is a transitional economy. It suffered from the combined results of political upheaval, the Serbian dismissal of Kosovo employees and the following <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a>. Despite declining foreign assistance, the GDP has mostly grown since its declaration of independence. This was despite the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">financial crisis of 2007–2008</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/European_debt_crisis" title="European debt crisis">European debt crisis</a>. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Inflation_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Inflation rate">inflation rate</a> has been low. Most economic development has taken place in the trade, retail and construction sectors. Kosovo is highly dependent on remittances from the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_diaspora" title="Albanian diaspora">diaspora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">FDI</a> and other capital inflows.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_Country_Report_No_12/100_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_Country_Report_No_12/100-221">[221]</a></sup> Kosovo is one of the poorest countries in Europe. In 2018, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> reported that approximately one-sixth of the population lived below the poverty line and one-third of the working age population was unemployed, the highest rate in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kosovo's largest trading partners are Albania, Italy, Switzerland, China, Germany and Turkey. The <a href="/wiki/Euro_currency" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro currency">Euro</a> is its official currency.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kosovo" title="Government of Kosovo">Government of Kosovo</a> has signed free-trade agreements with Croatia, Bosnia and Herzegovina, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-buyusa_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buyusa-227">[227]</a></sup> Kosovo is a member of <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central European Free Trade Agreement">CEFTA</a>, agreed with <a href="/wiki/UNMIK" class="mw-redirect" title="UNMIK">UNMIK</a>, and enjoys free trade with most nearby non-<a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Industry_of_Kosovo" title="Industry of Kosovo">secondary sector</a> accounted for 22.60% of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> and a general <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">workforce</a> of 800,000 employees in 2009. There are several reasons for this stagnation, ranging from consecutive occupations, political turmoil and the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Kosovo">War in Kosovo</a> in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-gjeografiaa77_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gjeografiaa77-229">[229]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Electrical_energy_in_Kosovo" title="Electrical energy in Kosovo">electricity sector</a> is considered as one of the sectors with the greatest potential of development.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> In April 2020 Kosovo with <a href="/wiki/KOSTT" title="KOSTT">KOSTT</a>, the government-owned Transmission System Operator, declared its independence from the Serbian electricity transmission operator <a href="/wiki/Elektromre%C5%BEa_Srbije" title="Elektromreža Srbije">Elektromreža Srbije</a> with a vote by the European Network of Transmission System Operators for Electricity, <a href="/wiki/ENTSO-E" class="mw-redirect" title="ENTSO-E">ENTSO-E</a>, which has paved the way for Kosovo to become an independent regulatory zone for electricity. The vote confirms that a connection agreement will be signed between ENTSO-E and KOSTT, allowing KOSTT to join the 42 other transmission operators. A joint energy bloc between Kosovo and Albania, is in work after an agreement which was signed in December 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> With that agreement Albania and Kosovo will now be able to exchange energy reserves, which is expected to result in €4 million in savings per year for Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> Kosovo has large reserves of lead, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, silver, <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, copper, iron and <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Natural_resources_key_to_the_future_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Natural_resources_key_to_the_future-233">[233]</a></sup> The nation has the 5th largest lignite reserves in the world and the 3rd in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> The Directorate for Mines and Minerals and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimated that Kosovo had €13.5&nbsp;billion worth of minerals in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo's_mineral_resources_at_13.5bn_euros_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo's_mineral_resources_at_13.5bn_euros-235">[235]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG/220px-Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG/330px-Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG/440px-Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Grapes from the <a href="/wiki/Orahovac" title="Orahovac">Orahovac</a> valley
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The primary sector is based on small to medium-sized family-owned dispersed units.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> 53% of the nation's area is agricultural land, 41% forest and forestry land, and 6% for others.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> The arable land is mostly used for corn, wheat, pastures, meadows and vineyards. It contributes almost to 35% of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> including the forestry sector. <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">Wine</a> has historically been produced in Kosovo. The wine industry is successful and has been growing after the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">war</a>. The main heartland of Kosovo's wine industry is in <a href="/wiki/Orahovac" title="Orahovac">Orahovac</a>, where millions of litres of wine are produced. The main cultivars include <a href="/wiki/Pinot_noir" title="Pinot noir">Pinot noir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merlot" title="Merlot">Merlot</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chardonnay" title="Chardonnay">Chardonnay</a>. Kosovo exports wines to Germany and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo's_wines_flowing_again_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo's_wines_flowing_again-238">[238]</a></sup> During the "glory days" of the wine industry, grapes were grown from the vineyard area of 9,000ha, divided into private and public ownership, and spread mainly throughout the south and west of Kosovo. The four state-owned wine production facilities were not as much "wineries" as they were "wine factories". Only the Rahovec facility that held approximately 36% of the total vineyard area had the capacity of around 50 million litres annually. The major share of the wine production was intended for exports. At its peak in 1989, the exports from the Rahovec facility amounted to 40&nbsp;million litres and were mainly distributed to the German market.<sup id="cite_ref-wine_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wine-239">[239]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kosovo" title="Tourism in Kosovo">Tourism in Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Brezovica_run.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Brezovica_run.jpg/220px-Brezovica_run.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Brezovica_run.jpg/330px-Brezovica_run.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Brezovica_run.jpg/440px-Brezovica_run.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Brezovica_run.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Brezovica_ski_resort" title="Brezovica ski resort">Brezovica ski resort</a> is one of the most visited winter tourist destinations in Kosovo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The natural values of Kosovo represent quality tourism resources. The description of Kosovo's potential in tourism is closely related to its geographical location, in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>. It represents a crossroads which historically dates back to <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">antiquity</a>. Kosovo serves as a link in the connection between <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. The mountainous west and southeast of Kosovo has great potential for winter tourism. Skiing takes place at the winter resort of <a href="/wiki/Brezovica_ski_resort" title="Brezovica ski resort">Brezovica</a> within the <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-turizmi_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turizmi-240">[240]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kosovo is generally rich in various topographical features, including high <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">canyons</a>, steep <a href="/wiki/Rock_formation" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock formation">rock formations</a> and <a href="/wiki/River" title="River">rivers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-turizmi_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turizmi-240">[240]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brezovica_ski_resort" title="Brezovica ski resort">Brezovica ski resort</a>, with the close proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Pristina_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Pristina Airport">Pristina Airport</a> (60&nbsp;km) and <a href="/wiki/Skopje_International_Airport" title="Skopje International Airport">Skopje International Airport</a> (70&nbsp;km), is a possible destination for international tourists. Other major attractions include the capital, <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>, the historical cities of <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peja" title="Peja">Peja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gjakova" title="Gjakova">Gjakova</a> but also <a href="/wiki/Ferizaj" title="Ferizaj">Ferizaj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gjilan" title="Gjilan">Gjilan</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a> included Kosovo on the list of 41 places to visit in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kosovo" title="Transport in Kosovo">Transport in Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Motorways_in_Kosovo" title="Motorways in Kosovo">Motorways in Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg/220px-Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg/330px-Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg/440px-Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3883" data-file-height="2591"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Pristina_International_Airport" title="Pristina International Airport">Pristina International Airport</a> (PRN) handles more than 2.1&nbsp;million passengers per year.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Currently, there are two main motorways in Kosovo: the <a href="/wiki/Albania%E2%80%93Kosovo_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Albania–Kosovo Highway">R7</a> connecting Kosovo with <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/R6_Motorway_(Kosovo)" class="mw-redirect" title="R6 Motorway (Kosovo)">R6</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> with the Macedonian border at <a href="/wiki/Elez_Han" title="Elez Han">Elez Han</a>. The construction of the new <a href="/wiki/R7.1_Motorway_(Kosovo)" class="mw-redirect" title="R7.1 Motorway (Kosovo)">R7.1 Motorway</a> began in 2017. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/R7_Motorway_(Kosovo)" class="mw-redirect" title="R7 Motorway (Kosovo)">R7 Motorway</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/Albania-Kosovo_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Albania-Kosovo Highway">Albania-Kosovo Highway</a>) links Kosovo to <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a> coast in <a href="/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs" title="Durrës">Durrës</a>. Once the remaining <a href="/wiki/European_route_E80" title="European route E80">European route (E80)</a> from <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> to <a href="/wiki/Merdare" title="Merdare">Merdare</a> section project will be completed, the motorway will link Kosovo through the present <a href="/wiki/European_route_E80" title="European route E80">European route (E80)</a> highway with the <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_corridor_X" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan-European corridor X">Pan-European corridor X</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_route_E75" title="European route E75">E75</a>) near <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="Niš">Niš</a> in Serbia. The <a href="/wiki/R6_Motorway_(Kosovo)" class="mw-redirect" title="R6 Motorway (Kosovo)">R6 Motorway</a> is currently under construction. Forming part of the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E65" title="European route E65">E65</a>, it is the second motorway constructed in the region and it links the capital <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> with the border with North Macedonia at <a href="/wiki/Elez_Han" title="Elez Han">Elez Han</a>, which is about 20&nbsp;km (12&nbsp;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>. Construction of the motorway started in 2014 and it is going to be finished in 2018. </p>
      <p>The nation hosts two airports, <a href="/wiki/Gjakova_Airport" title="Gjakova Airport">Gjakova Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pristina_International_Airport" title="Pristina International Airport">Pristina International Airport</a>. Gjakova Airport was built by the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">Kosovo Force</a> (KFOR) following the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, next to an existing airfield used for agricultural purposes, and was used mainly for military and humanitarian flights. The local and national government plans to offer Gjakova Airport for operation under a public-private partnership with the aim of turning it into a civilian and commercial airport.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Pristina International Airport is located southwest of <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>. It is Kosovo's only international airport and the only port of entry for air travelers to Kosovo. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Health care in Kosovo">Health in Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the past, Kosovo's capabilities to develop a modern <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> system were limited.<sup id="cite_ref-Sectorial_Health_Strategy_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectorial_Health_Strategy-244">[244]</a></sup> Low <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> during 1990 worsened the situation even more. However, the establishment of Faculty of Medicine in the <a href="/wiki/Universiteti_i_Prishtin%C3%ABs" class="mw-redirect" title="Universiteti i Prishtinës">University of Pristina</a> marked a significant development in health care. This was also followed by launching different health clinics which enabled better conditions for professional development.<sup id="cite_ref-Sectorial_Health_Strategy_244-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectorial_Health_Strategy-244">[244]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nowadays the situation has changed, and the health care system in Kosovo is organised into three sectors: <a href="/wiki/Primary_health_care" title="Primary health care">primary</a>, secondary and tertiary health care.<sup id="cite_ref-Sectorial_Health_Care_Strategy_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectorial_Health_Care_Strategy-245">[245]</a></sup> Primary health care in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> is organised into thirteen family medicine centres<sup id="cite_ref-prishtina-komuna.org_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prishtina-komuna.org-246">[246]</a></sup> and fifteen ambulantory care units.<sup id="cite_ref-prishtina-komuna.org_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prishtina-komuna.org-246">[246]</a></sup> Secondary health care is decentralised in seven regional hospitals. Pristina does not have any regional hospital and instead uses University Clinical Center of Kosovo for health care services. University Clinical Center of Kosovo provides its health care services in twelve clinics,<sup id="cite_ref-Stafi_i_QKUK-se_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stafi_i_QKUK-se-247">[247]</a></sup> where 642 doctors are employed.<sup id="cite_ref-2012_Health_Statistics_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012_Health_Statistics-248">[248]</a></sup> At a lower level, home services are provided for several vulnerable groups which are not able to reach health care premises.<sup id="cite_ref-Home_Services_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Home_Services-249">[249]</a></sup> Kosovo health care services are now focused on patient safety, quality control and assisted health.<sup id="cite_ref-Patient_Safety_and_Quality_Control_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patient_Safety_and_Quality_Control-250">[250]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kosovo" title="Education in Kosovo">Education in Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg/220px-Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg/330px-Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg/440px-Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5942" data-file-height="3967"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo" title="Academy of Sciences and Arts of Kosovo">Academy of Sciences and Arts</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>. Honorary members include the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_Americans" title="Albanian Americans">Albanian-American</a> Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Ferid_Murad" title="Ferid Murad">Ferid Murad</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in the Republic of Macedonia">Albanian</a> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> nun <a href="/wiki/Mother_Teresa" title="Mother Teresa">Mother Teresa</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education for primary, secondary, and tertiary levels is predominantly public and supported by the state, run by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Science_and_Technology_(Kosovo)" title="Ministry of Education, Science and Technology (Kosovo)">Ministry of Education</a>. Education takes place in two main stages: primary and secondary education and higher education. </p>
      <p>The primary and secondary education is subdivided into four stages: preschool education, primary and low secondary education, high secondary education and special education. Preschool education is for children from the ages of one to five. Primary and secondary education is obligatory for everyone. It is provided by gymnasiums and vocational schools and also available in languages of recognised minorities in Kosovo, where classes are held in <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>, Serbian, <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>. The first phase (primary education) includes grades one to five, and the second phase (low secondary education) grades six to nine. The third phase (high secondary education) consists of general education but also professional education, which is focused on different fields. It lasts four years. However, pupils are offered possibilities of applying for higher or university studies. According to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Science_and_Technology_(Kosovo)" title="Ministry of Education, Science and Technology (Kosovo)">Ministry of Education</a>, children who are not able to get a general education are able to get a special education (fifth phase).<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Higher education can be received in universities and other higher-education institutes. These educational institutions offer studies for <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">Bachelor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">Master</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">PhD</a> degrees. The students may choose full-time or part-time studies. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Kosovo">Media of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kosovo ranked 58th in the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> report compiled by the <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, while in 2016, it ranked 90th. The <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Kosovo">Media</a> consists of different kinds of communicative media such as radio, television, newspapers, and internet web sites. Most of the media survive from advertising and subscriptions. As according to IREX there are 92 radio stations and 22 television stations.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kosovo" title="Culture of Kosovo">Culture of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Kosovo" title="Architecture of Kosovo">Architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monuments_of_Kosovo" title="Monuments of Kosovo">Monuments of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_Albanian_heritage_in_Kosovo" title="Destruction of Albanian heritage in Kosovo">Destruction of Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_Serbian_heritage_in_Kosovo" title="Destruction of Serbian heritage in Kosovo">Serbian heritage in Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg/220px-Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg/330px-Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg/440px-Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2742" data-file-height="1823"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Hamam_of_Pristina" title="Great Hamam of Pristina">Great Hamam of Pristina</a> was built in the 15th century and was part of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Mosque_(Pristina)" title="Imperial Mosque (Pristina)">Imperial Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The architecture of Kosovo dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Age">Middle Ages</a>. It has been influenced by the presence of different civilisations and religions as evidenced by the structures which have survived to this day. </p>
      <p>Kosovo is home to many <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monasteries</a> and churches from the 13th and 14th centuries that represent the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox</a> legacy. Architectural heritage from the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Period</a> includes mosques and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_bath" title="Turkish bath">hamams</a> from the 15th, 16th and 17th centuries. Other historical architectural structures of interest include <a href="/wiki/Monuments_of_Kosovo" title="Monuments of Kosovo">kullas</a> from the 18th and 19th centuries, as well as a number of bridges, urban centers and fortresses. While some <a href="/wiki/Vernacular_architecture" title="Vernacular architecture">vernacular buildings</a> are not considered important in their own right, taken together they are of considerable interest. During the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">1999 conflict in Kosovo</a>, many buildings that represent this heritage were destroyed or damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-253">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unesco.org_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco.org-254">[254]</a></sup> In the Dukagjini region, at least 500 kullas were attacked, and most of them destroyed or otherwise damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-255">[255]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> recognised the <a href="/wiki/Visoki_De%C4%8Dani" title="Visoki Dečani">Visoki Dečani monastery</a> as <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> for its outstanding universal value. Two years later, the site of patrimony was extended as a serial nomination, to include three other religious monuments: <a href="/wiki/Patriarchate_of_Pe%C4%87_(monastery)" title="Patriarchate of Peć (monastery)">Patriarchate of Peja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Ljevi%C5%A1" title="Our Lady of Ljeviš">Our Lady of Ljeviš</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gra%C4%8Danica_monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Gračanica monastery">Gračanica monastery</a> under the name of <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Monuments_in_Kosovo" title="Medieval Monuments in Kosovo">Medieval Monuments in Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> It consists of four <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox</a> churches and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_monasteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian monasteries">monasteries</a>, which represent the fusion of the eastern Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine</a> and the western <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> ecclesiastical architecture to form the Palaiologian Renaissance style. The construction was founded by members of <a href="/wiki/Nemanji%C4%87_dynasty" title="Nemanjić dynasty">Nemanjić dynasty</a>, the most important dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="Serbia in the Middle Ages">Serbia in the Middle Ages</a>. </p>
      <p>These monuments have come under attack, especially during the <a href="/wiki/2004_unrest_in_Kosovo" title="2004 unrest in Kosovo">2004 ethnic violence</a>. In 2006, the property was inscribed on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_in_Danger" title="List of World Heritage in Danger">List of World Heritage in Danger</a> due to difficulties in its management and conservation stemming from the region's political instability.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kosovan art was unknown to the international public for a very long time, because of the regime, many artists were unable to display their art in art galleries, and so were always on the lookout for alternatives, and even resorted to taking matters into their own hands. Until 1990, artists from Kosovo presented their art in many prestigious worldwide renowned centers. They were affirmed and evaluated highly because of their unique approach to the arts considering the circumstances in which they were created, making them distinguished and original.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Congress2010_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Congress2010-259">[259]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 1979, the <a href="/wiki/Kosova_National_Art_Gallery" title="Kosova National Art Gallery">Kosova National Art Gallery</a> was founded. It became the highest institution of visual arts in Kosovo. It was named after one of the most prominent artists of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Mulliqi" title="Muslim Mulliqi">Muslim Mulliqi</a>. <a href="/wiki/Engj%C3%ABll_Berisha" title="Engjëll Berisha">Engjëll Berisha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masar_Caka" title="Masar Caka">Masar Caka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahir_Emra" title="Tahir Emra">Tahir Emra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_G%C3%ABrguri" title="Abdullah Gërguri">Abdullah Gërguri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hysni_Krasniqi" title="Hysni Krasniqi">Hysni Krasniqi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nimon_Lokaj" title="Nimon Lokaj">Nimon Lokaj</a>, Aziz Nimani, <a href="/wiki/Ramadan_Ramadani" title="Ramadan Ramadani">Ramadan Ramadani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esat_Valla" title="Esat Valla">Esat Valla</a> and Lendita Zeqiraj are some of few <a href="/wiki/List_of_Albanian_painters" title="List of Albanian painters">Albanian painters</a> born in Kosovo. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kosovan_cuisine" title="Kosovan cuisine">Kosovan cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ushqim_Tradicional_Flija.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Ushqim_Tradicional_Flija.JPG/220px-Ushqim_Tradicional_Flija.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Ushqim_Tradicional_Flija.JPG/330px-Ushqim_Tradicional_Flija.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Ushqim_Tradicional_Flija.JPG/440px-Ushqim_Tradicional_Flija.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1544" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ushqim_Tradicional_Flija.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Flia" title="Flia">Flia</a> is one of the most favored dishes of the traditional <a href="/wiki/Albanian_cuisine" title="Albanian cuisine">Albanian cuisine</a> in Kosovo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kosovan_cuisine" title="Kosovan cuisine">Kosovan cuisine</a> is mixed with influences of the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Albanians" title="Kosovo Albanians">Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Serbs" title="Kosovo Serbs">Serbian</a> origins of its majority population. Located at the crossroad of <a href="/wiki/Albanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian people">Albanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman people">Ottoman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Romance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic people">Slavic</a> cultures, Kosovo has enriched its own cuisine adopting and maintaining some of their cooking traditions and techniques. </p>
      <p>Food is an important component in the social life of the people of Kosovo particularly during <a href="/wiki/Religious_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious holiday">religious holidays</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>. For festive occasions, <a href="/wiki/Baklava" title="Baklava">Baklava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_delight" title="Turkish delight">Lokum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Halva" title="Halva">Halva</a> are traditionally prepared in almost every household throughout Kosovo and the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> regardless of ethnicity or cultural identity.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Perhaps the most prominent and traditional examples of Kosovan food include the <a href="/wiki/Flia" title="Flia">Flia</a> and Pite which are served with assorted <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fruit_preserves" title="Fruit preserves">fruit preserves</a>, honey and <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a>. Flia is composed of multiple layered <a href="/wiki/Crepe" class="mw-redirect" title="Crepe">crepe</a> and is predominantly brushed with cream while Pite are filled with a mixture of salty <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">cheese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a> or <a href="/wiki/Leek" title="Leek">leek</a>. </p>
      <p>The cuisine of Kosovo features a wide range of fresh <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herb" title="Herb">herbs</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bell_pepper" title="Bell pepper">red</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_pepper" title="Black pepper">black pepper</a> and vegeta.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Citation is a food company website. (November 2019)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The people of Kosovo enjoy a wide variety of meat and <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> products among other <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chicken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">kebab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sujuk" title="Sujuk">Sujuk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a> which is considered to be the traditional meat for religious occasions due to its religious connections. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">Tea</a> such as Albanian-style <a href="/wiki/Sideritis" title="Sideritis">mountain tea</a> or Russian and Turkish-style <a href="/wiki/Black_tea" title="Black tea">black tea</a> are a widely consumed beverage throughout Kosovo and particularly served at cafés, restaurants or at home. <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">Coffee</a> is another popular drink although Kosovo is steeped in culture and their coffee culture is a big part of the modern society.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Citation is an opinion piece. (November 2019)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Kosovo" title="Sport in Kosovo">Sport in Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_(cropped2).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG/180px-Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG/270px-Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="366"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_(cropped2).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Majlinda_Kelmendi" title="Majlinda Kelmendi">Majlinda Kelmendi</a>, an Olympic, World and European champion.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sport is a significant component of the society and culture of Kosovo. The most prominent sports in Kosovo include <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Committee_of_Kosovo" title="Olympic Committee of Kosovo">Olympic Committee of Kosovo</a> became a full member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Olympic_recognition_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olympic_recognition-263">[263]</a></sup> It participated at the <a href="/wiki/2015_European_Games" title="2015 European Games">2015 European Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/2019_European_Games" title="2019 European Games">2019 European Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>. </p>
      <p>By far the most popular <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sport</a> in Kosovo is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>. 1922 saw the founding of Kosovo's first clubs, including <a href="/wiki/KF_V%C3%ABllaznimi" title="KF Vëllaznimi">KF Vëllaznimi</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Prishtina" title="FC Prishtina">FC Prishtina</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> era from 1945 until 1991, football in <a href="/wiki/Former_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Former Yugoslavia">former Yugoslavia</a> advanced so rapidly that in 1946, the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Kosovo" title="Football Federation of Kosovo">Federation of Kosovo</a> was formed as a subsidiary of the Federation of Yugoslavia. Prishtina were the nation's most successful club during that period, spending five years in the top-tier <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_First_League" title="Yugoslav First League">Yugoslav First League</a> and reaching the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/1987-88_Yugoslav_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="1987-88 Yugoslav Cup">1987-88 Yugoslav Cup</a>. In 1991, an unsanctioned Kosovar league system known as the <i>Liga e Pavarur e Kosovës</i> ("Independent League of Kosovo") was set up, running parallel to the official Yugoslav leagues; in 1999, in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, this became <a href="/wiki/Ipko_Superliga" class="mw-redirect" title="Ipko Superliga">Kosovo's official league system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Football_in_Kosovo_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Football_in_Kosovo-264">[264]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Three footballers from Kosovo - <a href="/wiki/Milutin_%C5%A0o%C5%A1ki%C4%87" title="Milutin Šoškić">Milutin Šoškić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fahrudin_Jusufi" title="Fahrudin Jusufi">Fahrudin Jusufi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Durkovi%C4%87" title="Vladimir Durković">Vladimir Durković</a> - were part of the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslavia squad</a> that won a gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1960_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1960 Summer Olympics">1960 Summer Olympics</a> and a silver medal at the <a href="/wiki/1960_European_Nations%27_Cup" title="1960 European Nations' Cup">1960 European Championship</a>. Kosovar-born goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Stevan_Stojanovi%C4%87" title="Stevan Stojanović">Stevan Stojanović</a> became the first goalkeeper to captain a <a href="/wiki/European_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="European Cup">European Cup</a>-winning team when he captained <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_Belgrade" title="Red Star Belgrade">Red Star Belgrade</a> to victory in the <a href="/wiki/1991_European_Cup_Final" title="1991 European Cup Final">1991 European Cup Final</a>. </p>
      <p>The 2010s saw an increase in the number of <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in kosovo">Kosovar players of Albanian origin</a> playing in top European teams. These include <a href="/wiki/Lorik_Cana" title="Lorik Cana">Lorik Cana</a>, who captained <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Marseille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland A.F.C">Sunderland</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Albania_national_football_team" title="Albania national football team">Albanian national team</a>; <a href="/wiki/Valon_Behrami" title="Valon Behrami">Valon Behrami</a> who played for <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss national football team">Swiss national team</a>; <a href="/wiki/Xherdan_Shaqiri" title="Xherdan Shaqiri">Xherdan Shaqiri</a>, who won the <a href="/wiki/2018-19_UEFA_Champions_League" class="mw-redirect" title="2018-19 UEFA Champions League">2018-19 UEFA Champions League</a> with <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and also plays for Switzerland internationally;<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Adnan_Januzaj" title="Adnan Januzaj">Adnan Januzaj</a>, who began his career at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a> and currently represents <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a>. </p>
      <p>Basketball is also a popular sport in Kosovo. The first championship was held in 1991, with the participation of eight teams. The <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Federation_of_Kosovo" title="Basketball Federation of Kosovo">Basketball Federation of Kosovo</a> was accepted as a full member of <a href="/wiki/FIBA" title="FIBA">FIBA</a> on 13 March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Notable players born in Kosovo who played for the successful <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_basketball_team" title="Yugoslavia national basketball team">Yugoslavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbia national basketball team">Serbia national teams</a> include <a href="/wiki/Zufer_Avdija" title="Zufer Avdija">Zufer Avdija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marko_Simonovi%C4%87_(basketball,_born_1986)" title="Marko Simonović (basketball, born 1986)">Marko Simonović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Musli" title="Dejan Musli">Dejan Musli</a>, some of whom continue to competing for Serbia despite FIBA's recognition of Kosovo. </p>
      <p>Judoka <a href="/wiki/Majlinda_Kelmendi" title="Majlinda Kelmendi">Majlinda Kelmendi</a> became <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Judo_Championships" title="2013 World Judo Championships">World Champion</a> in 2013 and <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Judo_Championships" title="2014 World Judo Championships">2014</a>, and also the European Champion in <a href="/wiki/2014_European_Judo_Championships" title="2014 European Judo Championships">2014</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics 2016">Summer Olympics 2016</a>, Kelmendi became the first decorated Kosovan athlete to win a gold medal, also the first gold medal for Kosovo in a major sport tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-Olympics_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics-268">[268]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nora_Gjakova" title="Nora Gjakova">Nora Gjakova</a> won the first medal for Kosovo at the <a href="/wiki/2019_European_Games" title="2019 European Games">first European Games</a> in 2015, when she earned bronze in <a href="/wiki/Judo_at_the_2015_European_Games" title="Judo at the 2015 European Games">57 kg</a> category. In the <a href="/wiki/2019_European_Games" title="2019 European Games">second European Games</a> in 2019, Kelmendi won a gold medal, Gjakova a silver medal and <a href="/wiki/Loriana_Kuka" title="Loriana Kuka">Loriana Kuka</a> a bronze medal. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Kosovo" title="Music of Kosovo">Music of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:126px;max-width:126px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:134px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Rita_Ora_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg/124px-Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="124" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg/186px-Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg/248px-Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1497" data-file-height="1625"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:92px;max-width:92px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:134px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Rona_Nishliu.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rona_Nishliu.JPG/90px-Rona_Nishliu.JPG" decoding="async" width="90" height="136" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rona_Nishliu.JPG/135px-Rona_Nishliu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rona_Nishliu.JPG/180px-Rona_Nishliu.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <a href="/wiki/Rita_Ora" title="Rita Ora">Rita Ora</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> to <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in kosovo">Albanian</a> parents. (<i>left</i>) <a href="/wiki/Rona_Nishliu" title="Rona Nishliu">Rona Nishliu</a> represented <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Albania_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Albania in the Eurovision Song Contest 2012">2012 Eurovision Song Contest</a> where she finished 5th. (<i>right</i>)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although the music in Kosovo is diverse, authentic <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Albania" title="Music of Albania">Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian music">Serbian music</a> still exist. <a href="/wiki/Albanian_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian music">Albanian music</a> is characterised by the use of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%87ifteli" title="Çifteli">Çifteli</a>. <a href="/wiki/Classical_music_in_Kosovo" title="Classical music in Kosovo">Classical music</a> is well known in Kosovo and has been taught at several <a href="/wiki/List_of_pre-college_music_schools" title="List of pre-college music schools">music schools</a> and universities. In 2014, Kosovo submitted their first film for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film">Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Three_Windows_and_a_Hanging" title="Three Windows and a Hanging">Three Windows and a Hanging</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Isa_Qosja" title="Isa Qosja">Isa Qosja</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ThreeWindows_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThreeWindows-269">[269]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lahuta_QKVF.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lahuta_QKVF.jpg/180px-Lahuta_QKVF.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lahuta_QKVF.jpg/270px-Lahuta_QKVF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lahuta_QKVF.jpg/360px-Lahuta_QKVF.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4506"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lahuta_QKVF.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Gusle" title="Gusle">lahuta</a> is used by <a href="/wiki/Gheg_Albanians" class="mw-redirect" title="Gheg Albanians">Gheg Albanians</a> for the singing of epic songs or <a href="/wiki/Albanian_Songs_of_the_Frontier_Warriors" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian Songs of the Frontier Warriors">Albanian Songs of the Frontier Warriors</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the past, epic poetry in Kosovo and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Albania" title="Northern Albania">Northern Albania</a> was sung on a lahuta and then a more tuneful çiftelia was used which has two strings-one for the melody and one for drone. Kosovan music is influenced by Turkish music due to the almost 500-year span of Ottoman rule in Kosovo though Kosovan folklore has preserved its originality and exemplary.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> Archaeological research tells how old this tradition is and how it was developed in parallel with other traditional music in the Balkans. Roots dating to the 5th century BC have been found in paintings on stones of singers with instruments. (There is a famous portrait of "Pani" holding an instrument similar to a flute).<sup id="cite_ref-Kruta_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kruta-271">[271]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The contemporary music artists <a href="/wiki/Rita_Ora" title="Rita Ora">Rita Ora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dua_Lipa" title="Dua Lipa">Dua Lipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Era_Istrefi" title="Era Istrefi">Era Istrefi</a>, are all of <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanian origin</a> and have achieved international recognition for their music.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> One widely recognised musician from <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> is guitarist <a href="/wiki/Petrit_%C3%87eku" title="Petrit Çeku">Petrit Çeku</a>, winner of several international prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Serbian music from Kosovo presents a mixture of traditional music, which is part of the wider Balkan tradition, with its own distinctive sound, and various Western and Turkish influences.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt-274">[274]</a></sup> Serb songs from Kosovo were an inspiration for 12th song wreath by composer <a href="/wiki/Stevan_Mokranjac" title="Stevan Mokranjac">Stevan Mokranjac</a>. Most of Serbian music from Kosovo was dominated by church music, with its own share of sung epic poetry.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt_274-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt-274">[274]</a></sup> Serbian national instrument <a href="/wiki/Gusle" title="Gusle">Gusle</a> is also used in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Viktorija_(singer)" title="Viktorija (singer)">Viktorija</a> is the only artist from <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo" title="Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo">Kosovo</a> who represented <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Yugoslavia in the Eurovision Song Contest">Yugoslavia in the Eurovision Song Contest</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/Aska_(group)" title="Aska (group)">Aska</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_1982" title="Eurovision Song Contest 1982">1982</a>. Singer <a href="/wiki/Rona_Nishliu" title="Rona Nishliu">Rona Nishliu</a> finished 5th in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2012">2012</a> Eurovision Song Contest, while <a href="/wiki/Lindita_(singer)" title="Lindita (singer)">Lindita</a> represented Albania in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2017" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2017">2017</a>. Several Serbian singers from Kosovo have also participated in the Serbian national selection for the Eurovision Song Contest. <a href="/wiki/Nevena_Bo%C5%BEovi%C4%87" title="Nevena Božović">Nevena Božović</a> represented <a href="/wiki/Serbia_in_the_Junior_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Serbia in the Junior Eurovision Song Contest">Serbia in the Junior Eurovision Song Contest</a> and twice in the Eurovision Song Contest, firstly as a member of <a href="/wiki/Moje_3" title="Moje 3">Moje 3</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2013" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2013">2013</a> and as a solo act in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2019" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2019">2019</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Kosovo" title="Cinema of Kosovo">Cinema of Kosovo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg/180px-Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg/270px-Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg/360px-Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1109" data-file-height="1518"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bekim_Fehmiu" title="Bekim Fehmiu">Bekim Fehmiu</a> was the first Eastern European actor to star in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> during the Cold War.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The film industry of Kosovo dates from the 1970s. In 1969, the parliament of Kosovo established <i>Kosovafilm</i>, a state institution for the production, distribution and showing of films. Its initial director was the actor Abdurrahman Shala, followed by writer and noted poet Azem Shkreli, under whose direction the most successful films were produced. Subsequent directors of Kosovafilm were Xhevar Qorraj, Ekrem Kryeziu and Gani Mehmetaj. After producing seventeen feature films, numerous short films and documentaries, the institution was taken over by the Serbian authorities in 1990 and dissolved. Kosovafilm was reestablished after <a href="/wiki/FR_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="FR Yugoslavia">Yugoslav</a> withdrawal from the region in June 1999 and has since been endeavoring to revive the film industry in Kosovo. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kino-Kalaja.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kino-Kalaja.jpg/220px-Kino-Kalaja.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kino-Kalaja.jpg/330px-Kino-Kalaja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kino-Kalaja.jpg/440px-Kino-Kalaja.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="367"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kino-Kalaja.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dokufest" title="Dokufest">Dokufest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The International <a href="/wiki/Dokufest" title="Dokufest">Documentary and Short Film Festival</a> is the largest film event in Kosovo. The Festival is organised in August in <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>, which attracts numerous international and regional artists. In this annually organised festival, films are screened twice a day in three open-air cinemas as well as in two regular cinemas. Except for its films, the festival is also well known for lively nights after the screening. Various events happen within the scope of the festival: workshops, DokuPhoto exhibitions, festival camping, concerts, which altogether turn the city into a charming place to be. In 2010, Dokufest was voted as one of the 25 best international documentary festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>International actors of <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in kosovo">Albanian origin</a> from Kosovo include <a href="/wiki/Arta_Dobroshi" title="Arta Dobroshi">Arta Dobroshi</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Biberi" title="James Biberi">James Biberi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faruk_Begolli" title="Faruk Begolli">Faruk Begolli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bekim_Fehmiu" title="Bekim Fehmiu">Bekim Fehmiu</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Prishtina_International_Film_Festival" title="Prishtina International Film Festival">Prishtina International Film Festival</a> is the largest film festival, held annually in Pristina, in Kosovo that screens prominent international cinema productions in the Balkan region and beyond, and draws attention to the Kosovar film industry. </p>
      <p>The movie <a href="/wiki/Shok_(film)" title="Shok (film)">Shok</a> was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Live_Action_Short_Film" title="Academy Award for Best Live Action Short Film">Academy Award for Best Live Action Short Film</a> at the <a href="/wiki/88th_Academy_Awards" title="88th Academy Awards">88th Academy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> The movie was written and directed by Oscar nominated director <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Donoughue" title="Jamie Donoughue">Jamie Donoughue</a>, based on true events during the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo war">Kosovo war</a>. Shok's distributor is Ouat Media, and the social media campaign is led by <a href="/wiki/Team_Albanians" title="Team Albanians">Team Albanians</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> is an important fashion design, production, and trade hub in the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian-speaking</a> territories. </p>

               <tr>
                <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3">
                 <div>
                  <sup><small>1</small></sup> <span class="wrap">Kosovo is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008. <a href="/wiki/Kosovo%E2%80%93Serbia_relations" title="Kosovo–Serbia relations">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">2013 Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo is currently recognized as an independent state by <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">98</a> out of the 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">United Nations member states</a>. In total, <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113</a> UN member states recognized Kosovo at some point, of which <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">15</a> later withdrew their recognition.</span>
                 </div></td>
               </tr>

                   <ul>
                    <li><sup>1</sup> <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">Oceanic islands</a> within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.</li>
